Scope and FX were broadly neutral this quarter. As anticipated, the start of the year was challenging. No need to remind you that we are navigating in an uncertain macro environment with low visibility, and this does not support consumer confidence. Traffic was weak across most regions. Softer trends were observed in Western Europe, North America, and Japan, while they were consistent in Asia Pacific. Looking at the spending by nationalities, the slowdown was less pronounced, especially for the U.S. consumer. In Western Europe, both tourist and local trends decelerated versus Q4, but softness with locals had the biggest impact. The comparison base is also tough, and tourism spending kept weakening due to the less attractive pricing gap. Performance with locals was still subdued, but not more so than in Q4. Asia Pacific declined 25%, comparable fully in line with Q4. Greater China trends improve a touch sequentially on easier comps. The improvement is mostly led by mainland China. All-in-all, revenue from the Chinese cluster was down 27%, a bit better than in Q4. For their part, our other houses closed 11 net stores. In addition, Creed opened one store during the quarter.
